       <div class="col-sm-9 docs_page image_upload_api_reference">
        <div id="content">
         <nav class="breadcrumbs">
          <ul>
           <li class="false"><a href="/documentation">Documentation</a></li>
           <li>?</li>
           <li class="active"><a href="/documentation/image_upload_api_reference">Image upload API reference</a></li>
          </ul>
         </nav> 
         <h1> <span class="caption"> Image upload API reference </span> </h1> 
         <div class="docs_content"> 
          <p>The upload API consists of a number of methods for uploading and managing images in the cloud. The API methods can be called directly from within your own custom code or by using one of Cloudinary's SDKs that wrap the API and greatly simplify using its methods. </p> 
          <ul> 
           <li>Authenticated uploading is done over HTTPS using a secure protocol based on your account's <code>cloud_name</code>, <code>api_key</code> and <code>api_secret</code> parameters. When using Cloudinary's SDKs, these parameters are generally configured globally but they can be provided with each call instead. </li> 
           <li>Except where specifically noted, all information in the tables on this page apply equally to images, video, and raw files in all supported Frameworks. </li> 
           <li>Except where specifically noted, the parameter names are relevant for the HTTP API and all SDKs, although you may need to adjust the case style to fit the language you are working with. For example, for some languages, you may need to use <strong>camelCase</strong> or <strong>PascalCase</strong> instead of <strong>snake_case</strong>.</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p>The Upload API includes the following methods:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li><a href="#upload">Upload</a> - for uploading images to the cloud.</li> 
           <li><a href="#rename">Rename</a> - to rename an image (change its Public ID).</li> 
           <li><a href="#destroy">Destroy</a> - to delete an image.</li> 
           <li><a href="#tags">Tags</a> - for managing image tags.</li> 
           <li><a href="#context">Context</a> - for managing the context metadata attached to an image.</li> 
           <li><a href="#explicit">Explicit</a> - to update or apply actions to an already uploaded image.</li> 
           <li><a href="#explode">Explode</a> - to generate an image for each page in a PDF file.</li> 
           <li><a href="#generate_archive">Generate_archive</a> - to create or download an archive file (currently only ZIP supported).</li> 
           <li><a href="#generate_sprite">Generate_sprite</a> - for generating a single large image from multiple smaller images.</li> 
           <li><a href="#multi">Multi</a> - to create an animated GIF from multiple images.</li> 
           <li><a href="#text">Text</a> - to create an image from text.</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p>For more in depth documentation and general information on uploading images see the <a href="/documentation/upload_images">Upload images</a> documentation.</p>
          <p>For more information on calling the API methods directly, see the documentation on <a href="/documentation/upload_images#uploading_with_a_direct_call_to_the_api">Uploading with a direct call to the API</a>. </p>
          <p>SDK specific documentation can be found at:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li><a href="/documentation/rails_image_upload">Ruby on Rails</a></li> 
           <li><a href="/documentation/php_image_upload">PHP</a></li> 
           <li><a href="/documentation/django_image_upload">Django</a></li> 
           <li><a href="/documentation/node_image_upload">Node.js</a></li> 
           <li><a href="/documentation/java_image_upload">Java</a> </li> 
           <li><a href="/documentation/dotnet_image_upload">.NET</a></li> 
           <li><a href="/documentation/jquery_image_upload">jQuery</a></li> 
          </ul> 
          <p><strong>Note</strong>: After you upload files, you can use the Cloudinary Admin API, which has useful methods for administering and organizing your image files, such as listing all uploaded images, listing tags, finding all images that share a given tag, updating transformations, bulk deleting, and more. See the <a href="/documentation/admin_api">documentation on the Cloudinary Admin API</a> for more information.</p>
          <a class="anchor" name="upload"></a>
          <h3><a href="#upload">Upload</a></h3>
          <p>The <code>upload</code> method is used to upload resources to the cloud. </p>
          <p>For additional information and examples, see the <a href="/documentation/upload_images">uploading images</a> and <a href="/documentation/upload_videos">uploading videos</a> documentation.</p>
          <h5>Syntax:</h5>
          <div class="example multi_code ">
           <div class="framework_links">
            <a href="#api_example_1" class="active" data-framework="ruby">Ruby</a>
            <a href="#api_example_1" class="" data-framework="php">PHP</a>
            <a href="#api_example_1" class="" data-framework="python">Python</a>
            <a href="#api_example_1" class="" data-framework="nodejs">Node.js</a>
            <a href="#api_example_1" class="" data-framework="java">Java</a>
            <a href="#api_example_1" class="" data-framework="endpoint">Endpoint</a>
            <a href="#api_example_1" class=" sample_all" data-framework="all">All</a>
           </div>
           <a class="anchor" name="api_example_1"></a>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample active" data-framework="ruby">
            <div class="framework_name">
             Ruby:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>result = <span class="constant">Cloudinary</span>::<span class="constant">Uploader</span>.upload(file, options = {})</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="php">
            <div class="framework_name">
             PHP:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre><span class="local-variable">$result</span> = \<span class="constant">Cloudinary</span>\<span class="constant">Uploader</span>::upload(<span class="local-variable">$file</span>, <span class="local-variable">$options</span> = <span class="predefined">array</span>());</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="python">
            <div class="framework_name">
             Python:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>result = cloudinary.uploader.upload(<span class="predefined">file</span>, **options)</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="nodejs">
            <div class="framework_name">
             Node.js:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>cloudinary.v2.uploader.upload(file, options, callback);</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="java">
            <div class="framework_name">
             Java:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre><span class="predefined-type">Map</span> result = cloudinary.uploader().upload(<span class="predefined-type">String</span> file, <span class="predefined-type">Map</span> options);</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="endpoint">
            <div class="framework_name">
             Endpoint:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>https://api.cloudinary.com/v1_1/&lt;cloud_name&gt;/&lt;resource_type&gt;/upload</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <h5>Required parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>file</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The file to upload. It can be: 
              <ul>
               <li>a local file path (supported in SDKs only)</li>
               <li>the actual data (byte array buffer). <br>For example, in some SDKs, this could be an IO input stream of the data (e.g., File.open(file, "rb")). </li>
               <li>the Data URI (Base64 encoded), max ~60MB (62,910,000 chars)</li>
               <li>the remote FTP, HTTP or HTTPS URL address of an existing file</li>
               <li>an S3 URL of a whitelisted bucket</li>
              </ul>For details and examples, see: <a href="/documentation/upload_images#data_upload_options">data upload options</a></td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Optional parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td><code>Naming and storage:</code></td> 
             <td></td> 
             <td></td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>public_id</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The identifier that is used for accessing the uploaded resource. A randomly generated ID is assigned if not specified. The Public ID may contain a full path including folders separated by a slash (<code>/</code>). <br><strong>Note</strong>: The public ID value for images and resources should not include a file extension. Include the file extension for <code>raw</code> files only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>folder</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An optional folder name where the uploaded resource will be stored. The Public ID contains the full path of the uploaded resource, including the folder name.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>use_filename</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to use the original file name of the uploaded resource if available for the Public ID. The file name is normalized and random characters are appended to ensure uniqueness. Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>unique_filename</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>When set to false, should not add random characters at the end of the filename that guarantee its uniqueness. Only relevant if <code>use_filename</code> is also set to true. Default: <code>true</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>resource_type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Set the type of file uploading or <code>auto</code> to automatically detect the file type. Only relevant as a parameter when using the SDKs (the resource type is included in the endpoint URL for direct calls to the API). Valid values: <code>image</code>, <code>raw</code>, <code>video</code> and <code>auto</code>. Defaults: <code>image</code> for server-side uploading and <code>auto</code> for client-side uploading.<br><br><strong>Note</strong>: Use the <code>video</code> resource type for all video resources as well as for audio files, such as <code>.mp3</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Allows uploading resources as 'private' or 'authenticated' instead of the default public mode. Only relevant as a parameter when using the SDKs (the type is included in the endpoint URL for direct calls to the API). Valid values: <code>upload</code>, <code>private</code> and <code>authenticated</code>. Default: <code>upload</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>access_mode</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Allows the resource to behave as if it's of the authenticated 'type' (see above) while still using the default 'upload' type in delivery URLs. The image can later be made public by changing its access_mode via the <a href="/documentation/admin_api#update_access_mode">Admin API</a>, without having to update any image delivery URLs. Valid values: <code>public</code>, and <code>authenticated</code>. Default: <code>public</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>discard_original_filename</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to discard the name of the original uploaded file. Relevant when delivering resources as attachments (setting the <code>flag</code> transformation parameter to <code>attachment</code>). Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>overwrite</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to overwrite existing resources with the same Public ID. When set to false, return immediately if a resource with the same Public ID was found. Default: <code>true</code> (when using unsigned upload, the default is false and cannot be changed to true).</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>Resource data:</code></td> 
             <td></td> 
             <td></td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>tags</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An array (using the SDKs) or comma-separated list (for direct API calls) of tag names to assign to the uploaded resource for later group reference.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>context</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>A map (using the SDKs) or pipe-separated list (for direct API calls) of the key-value pairs of general textual context metadata to attach to an uploaded resource. The context values of uploaded files are available for fetching using the Admin API. For example: <code>alt=My image?caption=Profile image</code> (the <code>=</code> and <code>?</code> characters can be supported as values when escaped with a prepended backslash (<code>\</code>)). Note that key values are limited to 1024 characters.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>colors</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to retrieve predominant colors &amp; color histogram of the uploaded image. <br><strong>Note</strong>:If all returned colors are opaque, then 6-digit RGB hex values are returned. If one or more colors contain an alpha channel, then 8-digit RGBA hex quadruplet values are returned. <br>Default: <code>false</code>. Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>faces</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to return the coordinates of faces contained in an uploaded image (automatically detected or manually defined). Each face is specified by the X &amp; Y coordinates of the top left corner and the width &amp; height of the face. The coordinates for each face are returned as an array (using the SDKs) or a comma-separated list (for direct API calls), and individual faces are separated with a pipe (<code>?</code>). For example: <code>10,20,150,130?213,345,82,61</code>. <br>Default: <code>false</code>. Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>image_metadata</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to return IPTC, XMP, and detailed Exif metadata of the uploaded resource in the response. <br>Default: <code>false</code>. Relevant for images only.<br>(In .NET SDK, parameter name is <code>Metadata</code>.)</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>phash</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to return the perceptual hash (pHash) on the uploaded image. The pHash acts as a fingerprint that allows checking image similarity. <br>Default: <code>false</code>. Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>responsive_breakpoints</td> 
             <td>JSON</td> 
             <td>Requests that Cloudinary automatically find the best breakpoints. The parameter value is an an array of breakpoint request settings, where each request setting can include the following parameters: <code>create_derived</code>, <code>transformation</code>, <code>max_width</code>, <code>min_width</code>, <code>bytes_step</code>, <code>max_images</code> (see the table below for more information). The return response will include an array of the selected breakpoints for each breakpoint request, where the following information is given for each breakpoint: <code>width</code>, <code>height</code>, <code>bytes</code>, <code>url</code> and <code>secure_url</code>. <br>Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>auto_tagging</td> 
             <td>Decimal</td> 
             <td>Whether to assign tags to an image according to detected scene categories with a confidence score higher than the given value (between 0.0 and 1.0). See the <a href="/documentation/imagga_auto_tagging_addon">Imagga Auto Tagging</a>, <a href="aws_rekognition_auto_tagging_addon">Amazon Rekognition Auto Tagging</a>, and <a href="aws_rekognition_celebrity_and_face_detection_addon">Amazon Rekognition Celebrity Detection</a> add-ons for more details.<br>Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>categorization</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Set to <code>imagga_tagging</code> or <code>aws_rek_tagging</code> to automatically classify the scenes of the uploaded image. See the <a href="/documentation/imagga_auto_tagging_addon">Imagga Auto Tagging</a> and <a href="aws_rekognition_auto_tagging_addon">Amazon Rekognition Auto Tagging</a> add-ons for more details.<br>Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>detection</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Set to <code>adv_face</code> or <code>aws_rek_face</code> to extract an extensive list of face attributes from a photo using the <a href="/documentation/advanced_facial_attributes_detection_addon">Advanced Facial Attribute Detection</a> or <a href="aws_rekognition_celebrity_and_face_detection_addon">Amazon Rekognition Celebrity Detection</a> add-ons.<br>Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>ocr</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Set to <code>adv_ocr</code> to extract all text elements in an image as well as the bounding box coordinates of each detected element using the <a href="/documentation/ocr_text_detection_and_extraction_addon">OCR text detection and extraction add-on</a>.<br>Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>exif</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to retrieve the Exif metadata of the uploaded photo. Default: false. <strong>Deprecated - use image_metadata instead</strong></td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>Manipulations:</code></td> 
             <td></td> 
             <td></td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>eager</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An array (using the SDKs) or pipe-separated list (for direct API calls) of transformation representations. This generates derived resources in advance, instead of lazily creating each of the derived resources when first accessed by your site's visitors. <br>(In .NET SDK, parameter name is <code>EagerTransforms</code>.)</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>eager_async</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to generate the eager transformations asynchronously in the background after the upload request is completed rather than online as part of the upload call. Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>eager_notification_url</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An HTTP or HTTPS URL to send a notification to (a webhook) when the generation of eager transformations is completed.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>transformation</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An incoming transformation to run on the uploaded resource before saving it in the cloud. Using the SDKs, this parameter is given as a hash of transformation parameters (or an array of hashes for chained transformations), and for direct API calls it is given as a string of comma-separated single characters (separated with a slash for chained transformations). Note that when using the SDK for a dynamically-typed language, the transformation parameters can be specified directly without using this <code>transformation</code> parameter.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>format</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An optional format to convert the uploaded resource to before saving in the cloud. For example: <code>jpg</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>custom_coordinates</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Sets the coordinates of a single region contained in an uploaded image that is subsequently used for cropping uploaded images using the <code>custom</code> gravity mode. The region is specified by the X &amp; Y coordinates of the top left corner and the width &amp; height of the region, as an array (using the SDKs) or comma-separated list (for direct API calls). For example: <code>85,120,220,310</code>. <br>Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>face_coordinates</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Sets the coordinates of faces contained in an uploaded image and overrides the automatically detected faces. Each face is specified by the X &amp; Y coordinates of the top left corner and the width &amp; height of the face. The coordinates for each face are given as an array (using the SDKs) or a comma-separated list (for direct API calls) with individual faces separated with a pipe (<code>?</code>). For example: <code>10,20,150,130?213,345,82,61</code>. <br>Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>background_removal</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Set to <code>remove_the_background</code> to automatically clear the background of an image using the <a href="/documentation/remove_the_background_image_editing_addon">Remove-The-Background Editing add-on</a>.<br>Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>raw_convert</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Set to <code>aspose</code> to automatically convert Office documents to PDF files and other image formats using the <a href="/documentation/aspose_document_conversion_addon">Aspose Document Conversion add-on</a>.<br>Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td><code>Additional options:</code></td> 
             <td></td> 
             <td></td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>allowed_formats</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An array (using the SDKs) or comma-separated list (for direct API calls) of file formats that are allowed for uploading. Files of other types will be rejected. The formats can be any combination of image types, video formats or raw file extensions. For example: <code>mp4,ogv,jpg,png,pdf</code>. Default: any supported format for images and videos, and any kind of raw file (i.e. no restrictions by default).</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>async</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Tells Cloudinary whether to perform the upload request in the background (asynchronously). Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>backup</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Tell Cloudinary whether to backup the uploaded resource. Overrides the default backup settings of your account.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>callback</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>A URL to redirect to after the upload is completed instead of returning the upload response. Signed upload result parameters are added to the callback URL. This parameter is ignored for XHR (Ajax XMLHttpRequest) upload requests. <br><strong>Note</strong>: This parameter is relevant for direct uploads from a form in the browser. It is automatically set if you perform direct upload from the browser using Cloudinary's SDKs and the JQuery plugin.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>headers</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An HTTP header or a list of headers lines for returning as response HTTP headers when delivering the uploaded resource to your users. Supported headers: <code>Link</code>, <code>X-Robots-Tag</code>. For example: <code>X-Robots-Tag: noindex</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>invalidate</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to invalidate CDN cached copies of a previously uploaded resource (and all transformed versions that share the same Public ID). Default: <code>false</code>. <br> Note that it usually takes a few minutes (although it might take up to an hour) for the invalidation to fully propagate through the CDN. There are also a number of other <a href="/documentation/upload_images#invalidating_cached_images_on_the_cdn">important considerations</a> when using the invalidate functionality.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>moderation</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td><strong>For all resource types</strong>: Set to <code>manual</code> to add the uploaded resource to a queue of pending resources that can be moderated using the Admin API or the <a href="https://cloudinary.com/console/media_library" data-popup="true">Cloudinary Management Console</a>, or set to <code>metascan</code> to automatically moderate the uploaded resource using the <a href="metascan_anti_malware_protection_addon">Metascan Anti-malware Protection add-on</a>. <br><strong>For images only</strong>: Set to <code>webpurify</code> or <code>aws_rek</code> to automatically moderate the uploaded image using the <a href="webpurify_image_moderation_addon">WebPurify Image Moderation add-on</a> or the <a href="aws_rekognition_ai_moderation_addon">Amazon Rekognition AI Moderation add-on</a> respectively.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>notification_url</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An HTTP or HTTPS URL to receive the upload response (a webhook) when the upload is completed or a notification when any requested asynchronous action is completed.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>proxy</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Tells Cloudinary to upload resources from remote URLs through the given proxy. Format: <code>http://hostname:port</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>return_delete_token</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to return a deletion token in the upload response. The token can be used to delete the uploaded resource within 10 minutes using an unauthenticated API request. Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>upload_preset</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Name of an upload preset that you defined for your Cloudinary account. An upload preset consists of upload parameters centrally managed using the Admin API or from the <a href="https://cloudinary.com/console/settings/upload" data-popup="true">settings page of the management console</a>. An upload preset may be marked as unsigned, which allows unsigned uploading directly from the browser and restricts the directly allowed parameters to: <code>public_id</code>, <code>folder</code>, <code>tags</code>, <code>context</code>, <code>face_coordinates</code> and <code>custom_coordinates</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <p><a class="anchor" name="unsigned_upload_parameters"></a></p>
          <h5>Unsigned upload parameters</h5>
          <p>Unsigned requests are restricted to the following allowed parameters: <code>public_id</code>, <code>folder</code>, <code>callback</code>, <code>tags</code>, <code>context</code>, <code>face_coordinates</code> (images only), <code>custom_coordinates</code> (images only), and <code>upload_preset</code>. Most of the other upload parameters can be defined in your <code>upload_preset</code>.</p>
          <p>Additionally, although the <code>public_id</code> parameter can be specified, the <code>overwrite</code> parameter is always set to 'false' for unsigned uploads to prevent overwriting existing files.</p>
          <h5>responsive_breakpoints parameter request settings:</h5>
          <p>The responsive_breakpoints parameter accepts an array of breakpoint request settings, where <strong>each</strong> request setting includes the following parameters: </p>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>create_derived</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>(Required) If true, create and keep the derived images of the selected breakpoints during the API call. If false, images generated during the analysis process are thrown away.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>format</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>(Optional) Sets the file extension of the derived resources to the format indicated (as opposed to changing the format as part of a transformation - which would be included as part of the transformation component (e.g., f_jpg)).</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>transformation</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>(Optional) The base transformation to first apply to the image before finding the best breakpoints. The API accepts a string representation of a chained transformation (same as the regular transformation parameter of the upload API).</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>max_width</td> 
             <td>Integer</td> 
             <td>(Optional) The maximum width needed for this image. If specifying a width bigger than the original image, the width of the original image is used instead. Default: <code>1000</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>min_width</td> 
             <td>Integer</td> 
             <td>(Optional) The minimum width needed for this image. Default: <code>50</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>bytes_step</td> 
             <td>Integer</td> 
             <td>(Optional) The minimum number of bytes between two consecutive breakpoints (images). Default: <code>20000</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>max_images</td> 
             <td>Integer</td> 
             <td>(Optional) The maximum number of breakpoints to find, between 3 and 200. This means that there might be size differences bigger than the given bytes_step value between consecutive images. Default: <code>20</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>

          <p>To upload an image from a remote FTP private server <code>ftp://ftp.example.com/sample.jpg</code> with a username of <code>user1</code> and a password of <code>mypass</code>. Two transformed images are also eagerly generated as follows: </p> 
          <ol> 
           <li>Pad to a width of 400 pixels and height of 300 pixels.</li> 
           <li>Crop to a width of 260 pixels and a height of 200 pixels with north gravity. </li> 
          </ol> 
          <div class="example multi_code ">
           <div class="framework_links">
            <a href="#api_example_3" class="active" data-framework="ruby">Ruby</a>

            <span class="symbol">:eager</span> =&gt; [
            {<span class="symbol">:width</span> =&gt; <span class="integer">400</span>, <span class="symbol">:height</span> =&gt; <span class="integer">300</span>, 
             <span class="symbol">:crop</span> =&gt; <span class="symbol">:pad</span>},

             <span class="symbol">:crop</span> =&gt; <span class="symbol">:crop</span>, <span class="symbol">:gravity</span> =&gt; <span class="symbol">:north</span>}])</pre>

           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="nodejs">
            <div class="framework_name">
             Node.js:

            <div class="code-holder ">

          <a class="anchor" name="rename"></a>
          <h3><a href="#rename">Rename</a></h3>
          <p>Renamed images are immediately and permanently updated in your cloud storage with the <code>rename</code> method. The existing URLs of renamed images and their associated derived images are no longer valid, although images and transformed images already downloaded by visitors of your web site might still be accessible for a certain period of time through cached copies on the CDN. </p>
          <p>To bypass the CDN caching, you can include the <code>invalidate</code> parameter in your POST request in order to also invalidate the cached copies of the image on the CDN. Note that it usually takes a few minutes (although it might take up to an hour) for the invalidation to fully propagate through the CDN. For details on invalidating images, see <a href="upload_images#invalidating_cached_images_on_the_cdn">Invalidating cached images on the CDN</a>. </p>
          <h5>Syntax:</h5>
          <div class="example multi_code ">
           <div class="framework_links">
            <a href="#api_example_4" class="active" data-framework="ruby">Ruby</a>
            <a href="#api_example_4" class="" data-framework="php">PHP</a>
            <a href="#api_example_4" class="" data-framework="python">Python</a>
            <a href="#api_example_4" class="" data-framework="nodejs">Node.js</a>
            <a href="#api_example_4" class="" data-framework="java">Java</a>
            <a href="#api_example_4" class="" data-framework="endpoint">Endpoint</a>
            <a href="#api_example_4" class=" sample_all" data-framework="all">All</a>
           </div>
           <a class="anchor" name="api_example_4"></a>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample active" data-framework="ruby">
            <div class="framework_name">
             Ruby:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>result = <span class="constant">Cloudinary</span>::<span class="constant">Uploader</span>.rename(from_public_id, to_public_id, options = {})</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="php">
            <div class="framework_name">
             PHP:
            </div>

             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre><span class="local-variable">$result</span> = \<span class="constant">Cloudinary</span>\<span class="constant">Uploader</span>::<span class="predefined">rename</span>(<span class="local-variable">$from_public_id</span>, <span class="local-variable">$to_public_id</span>, <span class="local-variable">$options</span> = <span class="predefined">array</span>());</pre>
               </div> 
              </div>

             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>https://api.cloudinary.com/v1_1/&lt;cloud_name&gt;/&lt;resource_type&gt;/rename</pre>
               </div>

            </div>
           </div>

          <h5>Required parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>from_public_id</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The current identifier of the uploaded image.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>to_public_id</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The new identifier to assign to the uploaded image.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Optional parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>resource_type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The type of file to rename. Only relevant as a parameter when using the SDKs (the resource type is included in the endpoint URL for direct calls to the API). Valid values: <code>image</code>, <code>raw</code>, and <code>video</code>. Default: <code>image</code>. <br><br><strong>Note</strong>: Use the <code>video</code> resource type for all video resources as well as for audio files, such as <code>.mp3</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The specific type of the resource. Only relevant as a parameter when using the SDKs (the type is included in the endpoint URL for direct calls to the API). Valid values: <code>upload</code>, <code>private</code> and <code>authenticated</code>. Default: <code>upload</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>to_type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The new type for the resource. Valid values: <code>upload</code>, <code>private</code> and <code>authenticated</code>. Default: the type remains the same as before.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>overwrite</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to overwrite an existing resource with the target Public ID. Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>invalidate</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to invalidate CDN cached copies of the image (and all its transformed versions). Default: <code>false</code>. <br> Note that it usually takes a few minutes (although it might take up to an hour) for the invalidation to fully propagate through the CDN. There are also a number of other <a href="/documentation/upload_images#invalidating_cached_images_on_the_cdn">important considerations</a> when using the invalidate functionality</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>

  <span class="key"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">bytes</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>: <span class="integer">1414789</span>,
  <span class="key"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">type</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>: <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">upload</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>,
  <span class="key"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">url</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>: <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">http://res.cloudinary.com/demo/image/upload/v1473597073/grand_canyon.jpg</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>,
  <span class="key"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">secure_url</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>: <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">https://res.cloudinary.com/demo/image/upload/v1473597073/grand_canyon.jpg</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>
}</pre>
             </div> 
            </div> 
           </div>
          </div>
          <a class="anchor" name="destroy"></a>
          <h3><a href="#destroy">Destroy</a></h3>
          <p>The <code>destroy</code> method is used to immediately and permanently delete a single image from your Cloudinary account (to delete multiple images see the Admin API <a href="/documentation/admin_api#delete_resources">Delete resources</a> method). Backed up images are not deleted, and any images and transformed images already downloaded by visitors to your website might still be accessible through cached copies on the CDN. </p>
          <p>To bypass the CDN caching, you can include the <code>invalidate</code> parameter in your POST request in order to also invalidate the cached copies of the image on the CDN. Note that it usually takes a few minutes (although it might take up to an hour) for the invalidation to fully propagate through the CDN. For details on invalidating images, see <a href="upload_images#invalidating_cached_images_on_the_cdn">Invalidating cached images on the CDN</a>. </p>
          <h5>Syntax:</h5>
          <div class="example multi_code ">
           <div class="framework_links">
            <a href="#api_example_6" class="active" data-framework="ruby">Ruby</a>
            <a href="#api_example_6" class="" data-framework="php">PHP</a>
            <a href="#api_example_6" class="" data-framework="python">Python</a>
            <a href="#api_example_6" class="" data-framework="nodejs">Node.js</a>
            <a href="#api_example_6" class="" data-framework="java">Java</a>
            <a href="#api_example_6" class="" data-framework="endpoint">Endpoint</a>
            <a href="#api_example_6" class=" sample_all" data-framework="all">All</a>
           </div>
           <a class="anchor" name="api_example_6"></a>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample active" data-framework="ruby">
            <div class="framework_name">
             Ruby:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>result = <span class="constant">Cloudinary</span>::<span class="constant">Uploader</span>.destroy(public_id, options = {})</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="php">
            <div class="framework_name">
             PHP:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre><span class="local-variable">$result</span> = \<span class="constant">Cloudinary</span>\<span class="constant">Uploader</span>::destroy(<span class="local-variable">$public_id</span>, <span class="local-variable">$options</span> = <span class="predefined">array</span>());</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="python">
            <div class="framework_name">

            </div>

               </div>

             </div>

            </div>

             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>https://api.cloudinary.com/v1_1/&lt;cloud_name&gt;/&lt;resource_type&gt;/destroy</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <h5>Required parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>public_id</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The identifier of the uploaded image. <br><strong>Note</strong>: The public ID value for images and resources should not include a file extension. Include the file extension for <code>raw</code> files only.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Optional parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>resource_type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The type of file to destroy. Only relevant as a parameter when using the SDKs (the resource type is included in the endpoint URL for direct calls to the API). Valid values: <code>image</code>, <code>raw</code>, and <code>video</code>. Default: <code>image</code>. <br><br><strong>Note</strong>: Use the <code>video</code> resource type for all video resources as well as for audio files, such as <code>.mp3</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The specific type of the resource. Only relevant as a parameter when using the SDKs (the type is included in the endpoint URL for direct calls to the API). Valid values: <code>upload</code>, <code>private</code> and <code>authenticated</code>. Default: <code>upload</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>invalidate</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>If true, invalidates CDN cached copies of the image (and all its transformed versions). Default: <code>false</code>. <br> Note that it usually takes a few minutes (although it might take up to an hour) for the invalidation to fully propagate through the CDN. There are also a number of other <a href="/documentation/upload_images#invalidating_cached_images_on_the_cdn">important considerations</a> when using the invalidate functionality.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>

          <a class="anchor" name="tags"></a>
          <h3><a href="#tags">Tags</a></h3>
          <p>Tags are used to categorize and organize your images, and can also be used to apply group actions to images, for example to delete images, create sprites, ZIP files, JSON lists, or animated GIFs. Each image can be assigned one or more tags, which is a short name that you can dynamically use (no need to predefine tags).</p>
          <p>The <code>tags</code> method can be used to manage tags by directly calling the method and setting the value of the <code>command</code> parameter to either <code>add</code>, <code>remove</code>, <code>remove_all</code>, or <code>replace</code> tags. The Cloudinary SDKs wrap the tags method and offer 4 separate methods: one for adding tags, one for removing specific tags, one for removing all tags, and one for replacing tags.</p>
          <h5>Adding tags syntax:</h5>
          <div class="example multi_code ">
           <div class="framework_links">
            <a href="#api_example_8" class="active" data-framework="ruby">Ruby</a>
            <a href="#api_example_8" class="" data-framework="php">PHP</a>
            <a href="#api_example_8" class="" data-framework="python">Python</a>
            <a href="#api_example_8" class="" data-framework="nodejs">Node.js</a>
            <a href="#api_example_8" class="" data-framework="java">Java</a>
            <a href="#api_example_8" class="" data-framework="endpoint">Endpoint</a>
            <a href="#api_example_8" class=" sample_all" data-framework="all">All</a>
           </div>

           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="endpoint">
            <div class="framework_name">
             Endpoint:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>https://api.cloudinary.com/v1_1/&lt;cloud_name&gt;/&lt;resource_type&gt;/tags</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <h5>Required parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>tag</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The tag to assign, remove, or replace. Not relevant when removing all tags.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>public_ids</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>A list of Public IDs (up to 1000) of resources uploaded to Cloudinary.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>command</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>(Only relevant when using the API method directly - not for use with SDKs) The action to perform on resources: either <code>add</code> the given tag, <code>remove</code> the given tag, <code>remove_all</code> the tags assigned, or <code>replace</code> the given tag, which adds the given tag while removing all other tags assigned.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Optional parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>resource_type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The type of file. Only relevant as a parameter when using the SDKs (the resource type is included in the endpoint URL for direct calls to the API). Valid values: <code>image</code>, <code>raw</code>, and <code>video</code>. Default: <code>image</code>. <br><br><strong>Note</strong>: Use the <code>video</code> resource type for all video resources as well as for audio files, such as <code>.mp3</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The specific type of the resource. Only relevant as a parameter when using the SDKs (the type is included in the endpoint URL for direct calls to the API). Valid values: <code>upload</code>, <code>private</code> and <code>authenticated</code>. Default: <code>upload</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Examples:</h5>
          <p>To add the tag <code>animal</code> to the images with the Public IDs of <code>dog</code> and <code>lion</code></p>

            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>cloudinary.v2.uploader.replace_tag(<span class="string"><span class="delimiter">'</span><span class="content">animal</span><span class="delimiter">'</span></span>, [ <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">'</span><span class="content">dog</span><span class="delimiter">'</span></span>, <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">'</span><span class="content">lion</span><span class="delimiter">'</span></span> ],
        <span class="keyword">function</span>(result) { console.log(result) });</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>

        [<span class="string"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">dog</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>, <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">lion</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>], ObjectUtils.emptyMap());</pre>

               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <h5>Sample JSON response:</h5>
          <p>The following is a sample JSON response based on the example above. A tag was added to the <code>dog</code> and <code>lion</code> images. </p>
          <div class="code-holder ">
           <div class="code_inner">
            <div class="CodeRay"> 
             <div class="code">
              <pre>{
  <span class="key"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">public_ids</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>: [
    <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">dog</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>,
    <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">lion</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>
  ]
}</pre>
             </div> 
            </div> 
           </div>
          </div>
          <a class="anchor" name="context"></a>
          <h3><a href="#context">Context</a></h3>
          <p>The <code>context</code> parameter of an uploaded image contains a map (using the SDKs) or pipe-separated list (for direct API calls) of key-value pairs of general textual context metadata. The <code>context</code> method can be used to manage the context metadata of an uploaded image by directly calling the method and setting the value of the <code>command</code> parameter to either <code>add</code> a new key-value pair, or <code>remove_all</code> context metadata from the image. The Cloudinary SDKs wrap the context method and offer 2 separate methods: one for adding context and one for removing all context.</p>
          <h5>Adding context syntax:</h5>
          <div class="example multi_code ">
           <div class="framework_links">
            <a href="#api_example_16" class="active" data-framework="ruby">Ruby</a>
            <a href="#api_example_16" class="" data-framework="php">PHP</a>
            <a href="#api_example_16" class="" data-framework="python">Python</a>
            <a href="#api_example_16" class="" data-framework="nodejs">Node.js</a>
            <a href="#api_example_16" class="" data-framework="java">Java</a>
            <a href="#api_example_16" class="" data-framework="endpoint">Endpoint</a>
            <a href="#api_example_16" class=" sample_all" data-framework="all">All</a>
           </div>
           <a class="anchor" name="api_example_16"></a>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample active" data-framework="ruby">
            <div class="framework_name">
             Ruby:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>result = <span class="constant">Cloudinary</span>::<span class="constant">Uploader</span>.add_context(context, public_ids, options = {})</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="php">
            <div class="framework_name">
             PHP:
            </div>

              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre><span class="local-variable">$result</span> = \<span class="constant">Cloudinary</span>\<span class="constant">Uploader</span>::add_context(<span class="local-variable">$context</span>, <span class="local-variable">$public_ids</span>, <span class="local-variable">$options</span> = <span class="predefined">array</span>());</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>

            </div>
           </div>
          </div>

          <h5>Required parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>context</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>(Only relevant when adding context) A pipe-separated list (or map using the SDKs) of the key-value pairs of general textual context metadata to add to the image. The additional key-value pairs are merged with any existing context key-value pairs (if the key already exists then only the value is overwritten, and an empty value for an existing key clears the value). The <code>=</code> and <code>?</code> characters can be supported as values when escaped with a prepended backslash (<code>\</code>).</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>public_ids</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>A list of Public IDs of images uploaded to Cloudinary.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>command</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>(Only relevant when using the API method directly - not for use with SDKs) The action to perform on resources: either <code>add</code> the given context, or <code>remove_all</code> the context key-value pairs assigned.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Optional parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>resource_type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The type of file. Only relevant as a parameter when using the SDKs (the resource type is included in the endpoint URL for direct calls to the API). Valid values: <code>image</code>, <code>raw</code>, and <code>video</code>. Default: <code>image</code>. <br><br><strong>Note</strong>: Use the <code>video</code> resource type for all video resources as well as for audio files, such as <code>.mp3</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The specific type of the resource. Only relevant as a parameter when using the SDKs (the type is included in the endpoint URL for direct calls to the API). Valid values: <code>upload</code>, <code>private</code> and <code>authenticated</code>. Default: <code>upload</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>

          <a class="anchor" name="explicit"></a>
          <h3><a href="#explicit">Explicit</a></h3>
          <p>The <code>explicit</code> method is used to apply actions to already uploaded images, i.e., to update images that have already been uploaded. The most common usage of this method is to generate transformations for images that have already been uploaded, either so that they do not need to be generated on the fly when first accessed by users, or because <strong>Strict Transformations</strong> are enabled for your account and you cannot create transformed images on the fly (for more information, see <a href="/documentation/upload_images#control_access_to_images">Access control to images</a>). You can also use this method to pregenerate transformations for <a href="/documentation/image_transformations#fetching_images_from_remote_locations">remotely fetched images</a>. </p>
          <p>For more information see the documentation on <a href="/documentation/upload_images#update_already_uploaded_images">updating already uploaded images</a>.</p>
          <h5>Syntax:</h5>
          <div class="example multi_code ">
           <div class="framework_links">
            <a href="#api_example_20" class="active" data-framework="ruby">Ruby</a>
            <a href="#api_example_20" class="" data-framework="php">PHP</a>
            <a href="#api_example_20" class="" data-framework="python">Python</a>
            <a href="#api_example_20" class="" data-framework="nodejs">Node.js</a>
            <a href="#api_example_20" class="" data-framework="java">Java</a>
            <a href="#api_example_20" class="" data-framework="endpoint">Endpoint</a>
            <a href="#api_example_20" class=" sample_all" data-framework="all">All</a>
           </div>

          <h5>Required parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>public_id</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The identifier of the uploaded image or the URL of the remote resource. <br><strong>Note</strong>: The public ID value for images and resources should not include a file extension. Include the file extension for <code>raw</code> files only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The specific type of resource. Valid values for uploaded images: <code>upload</code>, <code>private</code>, or <code>authenticated</code>. Valid values for remote images: <code>fetch</code>, <code>facebook</code>, <code>twitter</code>, <code>gplus</code>, <code>instagram_name</code>, <code>gravatar</code>, <code>youtube</code>, <code>hulu</code>, <code>vimeo</code>, <code>animoto</code>, <code>worldstarhiphop</code> or <code>dailymotion</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Optional parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>eager</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>A list of transformations to create for the uploaded image, instead of lazily creating them when first accessed by your site's visitors (see the <a href="/documentation/image_transformation_reference">Image transformation reference</a> documentation for more details on possible values). This option accepts either a single transformation or an array of transformations (pipe-separated list for direct API calls) to create for the uploaded resource. <br>(In .NET SDK, parameter name is <code>EagerTransforms</code>.)</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>async</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Tells Cloudinary whether to perform the request in the background (asynchronously). Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>eager_async</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Determines whether to generate the eager transformations asynchronously in the background. Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>eager_notification_url</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An HTTP or HTTPS URL to notify your application (a webhook) when the generation of eager transformations is completed.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>tags</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An array (using the SDKs) or comma-separated list (for direct API calls) of tag names to assign to an image that replaces any current tags assigned to the image (if any).</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>invalidate</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to invalidate the image (and all its transformed versions) on the CDN. Default: <code>false</code>. <br> Note that it usually takes a few minutes (although it might take up to an hour) for the invalidation to fully propagate through the CDN. There are also a number of other <a href="/documentation/upload_images#invalidating_cached_images_on_the_cdn">important considerations</a> when using the invalidate functionality.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>context</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>A map (using the SDKs) or pipe-separated list (for direct API calls) of the key-value pairs of general textual context metadata to attach to an uploaded resource. The context values of uploaded files are available for fetching using the Admin API. For example: <code>alt=My image?caption=Profile image</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>headers</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An HTTP header or a list of headers lines for returning as response HTTP headers when delivering the uploaded resource to your users. Supported headers: <code>Link</code>, <code>X-Robots-Tag</code>. For example: <code>X-Robots-Tag: noindex</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>face_coordinates</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Sets the coordinates of faces contained in an uploaded image and overrides the automatically detected faces. Each face is specified by the X &amp; Y coordinates of the top left corner and the width &amp; height of the face. The coordinates for each face are given as an array (using the SDKs) or a comma-separated list (for direct API calls) with individual faces separated with a pipe (<code>?</code>). For example: <code>10,20,150,130?213,345,82,61</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>custom_coordinates</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Sets the coordinates of a region contained in an uploaded image that is subsequently used for cropping uploaded images using the custom gravity mode. The region is specified by the X &amp; Y coordinates of the top left corner and the width &amp; height of the region, as an array (using the SDKs) or comma-separated list (for direct API calls). For example: <code>85,120,220,310</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>notification_url</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An HTTP URL to send notification to (a webhook) when the upload is completed or any requested asynchronous action is completed.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>image_metadata</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to retrieve IPTC and detailed Exif metadata of the uploaded photo. Default: <code>false</code>. <br>(In .NET SDK, parameter name is <code>Metadata</code>.)</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>colors</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to retrieve predominant colors &amp; color histogram of the uploaded image. If one or more colors contain an alpha channel, then 8-digit RGBA hex quadruplet values are returned. <br>Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>phash</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to return the perceptual hash (pHash) on the uploaded image. The pHash acts as a fingerprint that allows checking image similarity. Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>faces</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to return the coordinates of faces contained in an uploaded image (automatically detected or manually defined). Each face is specified by the X &amp; Y coordinates of the top left corner and the width &amp; height of the face. The coordinates for each face are returned as an array (using the SDKs) or a comma-separated list (for direct API calls), and individual faces are separated with a pipe (<code>?</code>). For example: <code>10,20,150,130?213,345,82,61</code>. Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>raw_convert</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Set to <code>aspose</code> to automatically convert Office documents to PDF files and other image formats using the <a href="/documentation/aspose_document_conversion_addon">Aspose Document Conversion add-on</a>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>auto_tagging</td> 
             <td>Decimal</td> 
             <td>Whether to assign tags to an image according to detected scene categories with a confidence score higher than the given value (between 0.0 and 1.0). See the <a href="/documentation/imagga_auto_tagging_addon">Imagga Auto Tagging</a>, <a href="aws_rekognition_auto_tagging_addon">Amazon Rekognition Auto Tagging</a>, and <a href="aws_rekognition_celebrity_and_face_detection_addon">Amazon Rekognition Celebrity Detection</a> add-ons for more details.<br>Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>categorization</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Set to <code>imagga_tagging</code> or <code>aws_rek_tagging</code> to automatically classify the scenes of the uploaded image. See the <a href="/documentation/imagga_auto_tagging_addon">Imagga Auto Tagging</a> and <a href="aws_rekognition_auto_tagging_addon">Amazon Rekognition Auto Tagging</a> add-ons for more details.<br>Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>detection</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Set to <code>adv_face</code> or <code>aws_rek_face</code> to extract an extensive list of face attributes from a photo using the <a href="/documentation/advanced_facial_attributes_detection_addon">Advanced Facial Attribute Detection</a> or <a href="aws_rekognition_celebrity_and_face_detection_addon">Amazon Rekognition Celebrity Detection</a> add-ons.<br>Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>moderation</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td><strong>For all resource types</strong>: Set to <code>manual</code> to add the resource to a queue of pending resources that can be moderated using the Admin API or the <a href="https://cloudinary.com/console/media_library" data-popup="true">Cloudinary Management Console</a>, or set to <code>metascan</code> to automatically moderate the uploaded resource using the <a href="metascan_anti_malware_protection_addon">Metascan Anti-malware Protection add-on</a>. <br><strong>For images only</strong>: Set to <code>webpurify</code> or <code>aws_rek</code> to automatically moderate the image using the <a href="webpurify_image_moderation_addon">WebPurify Image Moderation add-on</a> or the <a href="aws_rekognition_ai_moderation_addon">Amazon Rekognition AI Moderation add-on</a> respectively.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>background_removal</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Set to <code>remove_the_background</code> to automatically clear the background of an image using the <a href="/documentation/remove_the_background_image_editing_addon">Remove-The-Background Editing add-on</a>.<br>Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>ocr</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Set to <code>adv_ocr</code> to extract all text elements in an image as well as the bounding box coordinates of each detected element using the <a href="/documentation/ocr_text_detection_and_extraction_addon">OCR Text Detection and Extraction add-on</a>.<br>Relevant for images only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>responsive_breakpoints</td> 
             <td>JSON</td> 
             <td>Requests that Cloudinary automatically find the best breakpoints. The parameter value is an an array of breakpoint request settings, where each request setting can include the following parameters: <code>create_derived</code>, <code>transformation</code>, <code>max_width</code>, <code>min_width</code>, <code>bytes_step</code>, <code>max_images</code> (see the table below for more information). The return response will include an array of the selected breakpoints for each breakpoint request, where the following information is given for each breakpoint: <code>width</code>, <code>height</code>, <code>bytes</code>, <code>url</code> and <code>secure_url</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>responsive_breakpoints parameter request settings:</h5>
          <p>The responsive_breakpoints parameter accepts an array of breakpoint request settings, where <strong>each</strong> request setting includes the following parameters: </p>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>create_derived</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>(Required) If true, create and keep the derived images of the selected breakpoints during the API call. If false, images generated during the analysis process are thrown away.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>format</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>(Optional) Sets the file extension of the derived resources to the format indicated (as opposed to changing the format as part of a transformation - which would be included as part of the transformation component (e.g., f_jpg)).</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>transformation</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>(Optional) The base transformation to first apply to the image before finding the best breakpoints. The API accepts a string representation of a chained transformation (same as the regular transformation parameter of the upload API).</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>max_width</td> 
             <td>Integer</td> 
             <td>(Optional) The maximum width needed for this image. If specifying a width bigger than the original image, the width of the original image is used instead. Default: <code>1000</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>min_width</td> 
             <td>Integer</td> 
             <td>(Optional) The minimum width needed for this image. Default: <code>50</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>bytes_step</td> 
             <td>Integer</td> 
             <td>(Optional) The minimum number of bytes between two consecutive breakpoints (images). Default: <code>20000</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>max_images</td> 
             <td>Integer</td> 
             <td>(Optional) The maximum number of breakpoints to find, between 3 and 200. This means that there might be size differences bigger than the given bytes_step value between consecutive images. Default: <code>20</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Example:</h5>
          <p>To explicitly create two transformed images for the already uploaded image with a Public ID of <code>sample</code> as follows: </p> 
          <ol> 
           <li>Crop to a width and height of 400 pixels including the biggest face detected. </li> 
           <li>Pad to a width of 660 pixels and a height of 400 pixels with a blue background. </li> 
          </ol>

            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>cloudinary.v2.uploader.explicit(<span class="string"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">sample</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>, 
    { <span class="key">type</span>: <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">upload</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>,
      <span class="key">eager</span>: [
        { <span class="key">width</span>: <span class="integer">400</span>, <span class="key">height</span>: <span class="integer">400</span>,
          <span class="key">crop</span>: <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">crop</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>, <span class="key">gravity</span>: <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">face</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>},

          <span class="key">crop</span>: <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">pad</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>, <span class="key">background</span>: <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">blue</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>} ]}, 
    <span class="keyword">function</span>(error, result) {console.log(result); });</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>

          <a class="anchor" name="explode"></a>
          <h3><a href="#explode">Explode</a></h3>
          <p>The <code>explode</code> method creates derived images for all of the individual pages in a PDF file. Each derived image is stored with the same Public ID as the PDF file, and can be accessed using the <code>page</code> parameter, in order to deliver the image of a specific PDF page (see the documentation on <a href="/documentation/image_transformations#creating_images_from_pdf_files">Creating images from PDF files</a>). </p>
          <p>You could deliver individual pages of a PDF on-the-fly without the <code>explode</code> method. This method is useful for pregenerating all the pages of the PDF as a chunk explicit transformation, so that they do not need to be generated on-the-fly when first accessed by your users.</p>
          <h5>Syntax:</h5>
          <div class="example multi_code ">
           <div class="framework_links">
            <a href="#api_example_22" class="active" data-framework="ruby">Ruby</a>
            <a href="#api_example_22" class="" data-framework="php">PHP</a>
            <a href="#api_example_22" class="" data-framework="python">Python</a>
            <a href="#api_example_22" class="" data-framework="nodejs">Node.js</a>
            <a href="#api_example_22" class="" data-framework="java">Java</a>
            <a href="#api_example_22" class="" data-framework="endpoint">Endpoint</a>
            <a href="#api_example_22" class=" sample_all" data-framework="all">All</a>
           </div>
