          <h5>Required parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>public_id</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The identifier of the uploaded PDF file. <br><strong>Note</strong>: The public ID value for images and resources should not include a file extension. Include the file extension for <code>raw</code> files only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>transformation</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>A transformation to run on all the pages before storing them as derived images. This parameter is given as an array (using the SDKs) or comma-separated list (for direct API calls) of transformations, and separated with a slash for chained transformations. <br><br>At minimum, you must pass the <code>page</code> transformation with the value <code>all</code>. If you supply additional transformations, you must deliver the image using the same relative order of the <code>page</code> and the other transformations. If you use a different order when you deliver, then it is considered a different transformation, and will be generated on-the-fly as a new derived image.<br><br>Note that when using the SDK for a dynamically-typed language, the transformation parameters can be specified directly without using this <code>transformation</code> parameter, as seen in the examples for Ruby, PHP, Python, and Node.js below.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Optional parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The specific file type of the resource. Valid values: <code>upload</code>, <code>private</code> and <code>authenticated</code>. Default: <code>upload</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>format</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An optional format to convert the images before storing them in your Cloudinary account. Default: <code>png</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>notification_url</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An HTTP or HTTPS URL to notify your application (a webhook) when the process has completed.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>

          <a class="anchor" name="generate_archive"></a>
          <h3><a href="#generate_archive">Generate_archive</a></h3>
          <p>The <code>generate_archive</code> method creates an archive file that contains all the images meeting specified tag, Public ID, or prefix criteria (or a combination thereof). The method can be used directly to either return the generated archive file ('download') or to store it as a raw resource in your Cloudinary account ('create'), by setting the value of the <code>mode</code> parameter. </p>
          <p>By default, if all the images in the archive have the identical transformation applied, they are stored in the archive with the original image filename only, regardless of the value of the <code>flatten_transformations</code> or <code>skip_transformation_name</code> parameters. If images with different transformations are included in the archive, then the relevant transformation data is appended to the filename of each image, according to the settings of the <code>flatten_transformations</code> or <code>skip_transformation_name</code> parameters.</p>
          <p>The archive can contain up to 1000 resources or 5000 derived images. The maximum archive file size is the larger of 100 MB or your account's <code>raw</code> file size limit. </p>
          <p>The Cloudinary SDKs wrap the generate_archive method and offer 4 separate methods: </p> 
          <ul> 
           <li><code>create_zip</code>: generates a ZIP file based on the given parameter values, uploads the file to your Cloudinary account, returns a JSON response with the URLs for accessing the ZIP file, and can then be delivered like any other <a href="upload_images#uploading_non_image_files_as_raw_files">raw file uploaded to Cloudinary</a>.</li> 
           <li><code>create_archive</code>: generates an archive file based on the given parameter values (default target_format = zip), uploads the file to your Cloudinary account, returns a JSON response with the URLs for accessing the archive file, and can then be delivered like any other <a href="upload_images#uploading_non_image_files_as_raw_files">raw file uploaded to Cloudinary</a>. </li> 
           <li><code>download_zip_url</code>: generates a signed URL that expires after 1 hour (by default). The URL can be accessed to dynamically create and then download a ZIP file based on the given parameter values. The resulting ZIP file is not cached or stored in your Cloudinary account.</li> 
           <li><code>download_archive_url</code>: generates a signed URL that expires after 1 hour (by default). The URL can be accessed to dynamically create and then download an archive file based on the given parameter values. The resulting archive file is not cached or stored in your Cloudinary account.</li> 
          </ul> 
          <h5>create_zip syntax:</h5>
          <div class="example multi_code ">
           <div class="framework_links">
            <a href="#api_example_24" class="active" data-framework="ruby">Ruby</a>
            <a href="#api_example_24" class="" data-framework="php">PHP</a>
            <a href="#api_example_24" class="" data-framework="python">Python</a>
            <a href="#api_example_24" class="" data-framework="nodejs">Node.js</a>
            <a href="#api_example_24" class="" data-framework="java">Java</a>

          <h5>Required parameters:</h5>
          <p>At least one of the following "filtering" parameters needs to be specified, in order to tell Cloudinary which resources to include in the archive file. Specifying any combination of the three parameters is also allowed - a unique union of all the matching resources will then be included in the archive file:</p>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>tags</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An array (using the SDKs) or comma-separated list (for direct API calls) of tag names. All images with the specified tags are included in the archive. Up to 20 tags are supported.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>public_ids</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An array (using the SDKs) or comma-separated list (for direct API calls) of Public IDs for the specific images to be included in the archive. Up to 1000 public IDs are supported.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>prefixes</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An array (using the SDKs) or comma-separated list (for direct API calls) of prefixes of Public IDs (e.g., folders). Setting this parameter to a slash (<code>/</code>) is a shortcut for including all images in the account for the given resource type and type (up to the max files limit). Up to 20 prefixes are supported.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Optional parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>resource_type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The resource type (<code>image</code>, <code>video</code> or <code>raw</code>) of files to include in the archive: Default: <code>image</code>. <br><br><strong>Note</strong>: The <code>video</code> resource type applies to video resources aand to audio files, such as <code>.mp3</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>type</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The specific file type of resources to include in the archive (<code>upload</code>/<code>private</code>/<code>authenticated</code>). If tags are specified as a filter then all types are included. Default: <code>upload</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>transformations</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>A transformation to run on all the derived images before storing them in your Cloudinary account. This parameter is given as an array (using the SDKs) or comma-separated list (for direct API calls) of transformations, and separated with a slash for chained transformations. Note that when using the SDK for a dynamically-typed language, the transformation parameters can be specified directly without using the <code>transformation</code> parameter. If this parameter is not specified then the original images are included in the archive.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>mode</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Determines whether to return a URL to dynamically generate and download the archive file (<code>download</code>) or to create and store it as a raw resource in your Cloudinary account and return a JSON with the URLs for accessing the archive file (<code>create</code>). Only relevant when using the API method directly - not for use with SDKs. Default: <code>create</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>target_format</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The format for the generated archive: <code>zip</code> or <code>tgz</code>. Only relevant when using the direct API call or the 'archive' SDK methods - not for use with the 'zip' SDK methods. Default: <code>zip</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>target_public_id</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The Public ID to assign to the generated archive. If not specified, a random Public ID is generated. Only relevant when using the 'create' SDK methods and the 'create' mode in direct calls.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>flatten_folders</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Determines whether to flatten all files to be in the root of the archive file (no sub-folders). Any folder information included in the Public ID is stripped and a numeric counter is added to the file name in the case of a name conflict. Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>flatten_transformations</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>If multiple transformations are also applied, determines whether to flatten the folder structure of the derived images and store the transformation details on the file name instead. Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>skip_transformation_name</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Determines whether to strip all transformation details from file names and add a numeric counter to a file name in the case of a name conflict. Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>allow_missing</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Allows generation of the archive if any of the supplied Public IDs are not found, instead of returning an error. Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>expires_at</td> 
             <td>Integer</td> 
             <td>The date (UNIX time in seconds) for the URL expiration (e.g., 1415060076). Only relevant when using the 'download' SDK methods and the 'download' mode in direct calls. Default: 1 hour from the time that the URL is generated.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>use_original_filename</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to use the original file name of the included images (if available) instead of the Public ID. Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>async</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to perform the archive generation in the background (asynchronously). Only relevant when using the 'create' SDK methods and the 'create' mode in direct calls. Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>notification_url</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An HTTP or HTTPS URL to notify your application (a webhook) when the archive creation process has completed. Only relevant when using the 'create' SDK methods and the 'create' mode in direct calls.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>target_tags</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An array (using the SDKs) or comma-separated list (for direct API calls) of tag names to assign to the generated archive. Only relevant when using the 'create' SDK methods and the 'create' mode in direct calls.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>keep_derived</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Whether to keep the derived images used for generating the archive. Default: <code>false.</code></td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Examples:</h5>
          <p>To create a zip file that contains all images that have the <code>lion</code> tag:</p>
          <div class="example multi_code ">
           <div class="framework_links">
            <a href="#api_example_28" class="active" data-framework="ruby">Ruby</a>
            <a href="#api_example_28" class="" data-framework="php">PHP</a>
            <a href="#api_example_28" class="" data-framework="python">Python</a>
            <a href="#api_example_28" class="" data-framework="nodejs">Node.js</a>
            <a href="#api_example_28" class="" data-framework="java">Java</a>
            <a href="#api_example_28" class="" data-framework="curl">cURL</a>
            <a href="#api_example_28" class=" sample_all" data-framework="all">All</a>
           </div>
           <a class="anchor" name="api_example_28"></a>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample active" data-framework="ruby">
            <div class="framework_name">
             Ruby:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre><span class="constant">Cloudinary</span>::<span class="constant">Uploader</span>.create_zip(
    <span class="symbol">:tags</span> =&gt; <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">'</span><span class="content">lion</span><span class="delimiter">'</span></span>, 
    <span class="symbol">:resource_type</span> =&gt; <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">'</span><span class="content">image</span><span class="delimiter">'</span></span>)</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="php">
            <div class="framework_name">
             PHP:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>\<span class="constant">Cloudinary</span>\<span class="constant">Uploader</span>::create_zip(
    <span class="predefined">array</span>(
        <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">'</span><span class="content">tags</span><span class="delimiter">'</span></span> =&gt; <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">'</span><span class="content">lion</span><span class="delimiter">'</span></span>, 
        <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">'</span><span class="content">resource_type</span><span class="delimiter">'</span></span> =&gt; <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">'</span><span class="content">image</span><span class="delimiter">'</span></span>));</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="python">
            <div class="framework_name">

            </div>

             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>cloudinary.uploader.create_zip(
    tags = <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">'</span><span class="content">lion</span><span class="delimiter">'</span></span>, 
    resource_type = <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">'</span><span class="content">image</span><span class="delimiter">'</span></span>)</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>

               <div class="code">
                <pre>cloudinary.v2.uploader.create_zip(
    { <span class="key">tags</span>: <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">'</span><span class="content">lion</span><span class="delimiter">'</span></span>, <span class="key">resource_type</span>: <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">'</span><span class="content">image</span><span class="delimiter">'</span></span>},

           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="java">

          <a class="anchor" name="generate_sprite"></a>
          <h3><a href="#generate_sprite">Generate_sprite</a></h3>
          <p>Cloudinary supports generating sprites by merging multiple images into a single large image for reducing network overhead and bypassing download limitations. The browser downloads only a single image and a CSS file that directs the browser to which part of the sprite to use for displaying each contained image. The <code>generate_sprite</code> method creates a sprite from all images that have been assigned a specified tag. The process produces 2 files as follows:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li>A single image file containing all the images with the specified tag (PNG by default).</li> 
           <li>A CSS file that includes the style class names and the location of the individual images in the sprite.</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p>For a detailed explanation on generating and using sprites, see the <a href="/documentation/sprite_generation">documentation on sprite generation</a>.</p>
          <h5>Syntax:</h5>
          <div class="example multi_code ">
           <div class="framework_links">
            <a href="#api_example_30" class="active" data-framework="ruby">Ruby</a>
            <a href="#api_example_30" class="" data-framework="php">PHP</a>
            <a href="#api_example_30" class="" data-framework="python">Python</a>
            <a href="#api_example_30" class="" data-framework="nodejs">Node.js</a>
            <a href="#api_example_30" class="" data-framework="java">Java</a>
            <a href="#api_example_30" class="" data-framework="endpoint">Endpoint</a>
            <a href="#api_example_30" class=" sample_all" data-framework="all">All</a>
           </div>
           <a class="anchor" name="api_example_30"></a>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample active" data-framework="ruby">
            <div class="framework_name">
             Ruby:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>result = <span class="constant">Cloudinary</span>::<span class="constant">Uploader</span>.generate_sprite(tag, options = {})</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="php">
            <div class="framework_name">
             PHP:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre><span class="local-variable">$result</span> = \<span class="constant">Cloudinary</span>\<span class="constant">Uploader</span>::generate_sprite(<span class="local-variable">$tag</span>, <span class="local-variable">$options</span> = <span class="predefined">array</span>());</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>

             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>https://api.cloudinary.com/v1_1/&lt;cloud_name&gt;/image/generate_sprite</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <h5>Required parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>tag</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The sprite is created from all images with this tag.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Optional parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>transformation</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>A transformation to run on all the individual images before creating the sprite. This parameter is given as as an array (using the SDKs) or comma-separated list (for direct API calls) of transformations, and separated with a slash for chained transformations. Note that when using the SDK for a dynamically-typed language, the transformation parameters can be specified directly without using this <code>transformation</code> parameter.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>format</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An optional format to convert the sprite before saving it in your Cloudinary account. Default: <code>png</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>async</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Tells Cloudinary whether to perform the sprite generation in the background (asynchronously). Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>notification_url</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An HTTP or HTTPS URL to notify your application (a webhook) when the process has completed.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Example:</h5>
          <p>Generating a sprite from all images tagged with <code>logo</code>, creates a single PNG image file with the Public ID of <code>logo</code> that contains all the tagged images, and a CSS file with the Public ID of <code>logo.css</code>. </p>

      <span class="key"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">y</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>: <span class="integer">167</span>
    },
    <span class="key"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">https://cloudinary.com/images/logo.png</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>: {
      <span class="key"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">width</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>: <span class="integer">165</span>,
      <span class="key"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">height</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>: <span class="integer">165</span>,
      <span class="key"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">x</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>: <span class="integer">0</span>,
      <span class="key"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">y</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>: <span class="integer">201</span>
    }
  }
}</pre>
             </div> 
            </div> 
           </div>
          </div>
          <a class="anchor" name="multi"></a>
          <h3><a href="#multi">Multi</a></h3>
          <p>The <code>multi</code> method creates a single animated GIF file from all images that have been assigned a specified tag, where each image is included as a single frame of the resulting animating GIF (sorted alphabetically by their Public ID). For a detailed explanation on generating animated GIFs, see the <a href="/documentation/image_transformations#creating_animated_gifs">documentation on creating animated GIFs</a>.</p>
          <p>Animated GIFs can be created from a maximum of 500 frames (individual images), except in the following cases where the limit is 100 frames maximum:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li>If the processing is done in a synchronous mode (i.e., without the <code>async</code> parameter set to true).</li> 
           <li>If there is a underlay or overlay added to the image (<code>l_</code> or <code>u_</code>).</li> 
           <li>If any transformation parameters are added that are not on the following list: <code>background</code>, <code>flags</code>, <code>crop</code>, <code>width</code>, <code>height</code>, <code>x</code>, <code>y</code>, <code>gravity</code>, <code>quality</code>, <code>angle</code>, <code>page</code>, and <code>dpr</code>.</li> 
           <li>If the <code>angle</code> parameter is added with a value that is anything but <code>exif</code> or <code>auto</code>.</li> 
           <li>If the <code>crop</code> parameter is added with a value that is anything but <code>scale</code>, <code>limit</code>, <code>fit</code>, <code>fill</code>, <code>thumb</code> or <code>crop</code>.</li> 
          </ul> 
          <h5>Syntax:</h5>
          <div class="example multi_code ">
           <div class="framework_links">
            <a href="#api_example_32" class="active" data-framework="ruby">Ruby</a>
            <a href="#api_example_32" class="" data-framework="php">PHP</a>
            <a href="#api_example_32" class="" data-framework="python">Python</a>
            <a href="#api_example_32" class="" data-framework="nodejs">Node.js</a>
            <a href="#api_example_32" class="" data-framework="java">Java</a>
            <a href="#api_example_32" class="" data-framework="endpoint">Endpoint</a>
            <a href="#api_example_32" class=" sample_all" data-framework="all">All</a>
           </div>

               </div>

          <h5>Required parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>tag</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The animated GIF is created from all images with this tag.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Optional parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>transformation</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>A transformation to run on all the individual images before creating the animated GIF. This parameter is given as an array (using the SDKs) or comma-separated list (for direct API calls) of transformations, and separated with a slash for chained transformations. Note that when using the SDK for a dynamically-typed language, the transformation parameters can be specified directly without using this <code>transformation</code> parameter.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>async</td> 
             <td>Boolean</td> 
             <td>Tells Cloudinary whether to perform the GIF generation in the background (asynchronously). Default: <code>false</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>format</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Can be set to 'zip' to generate a zip file containing the images instead of an animated GIF file. Default: <code>gif</code> (<strong>deprecated - use the new <a href="#generate_archive">generate_archive</a> method to create zip files</strong>)</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>notification_url</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>An HTTP or HTTPS URL to notify your application (a webhook) when the process has completed.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>

          <a class="anchor" name="text"></a>
          <h3><a href="#text">Text</a></h3>
          <p>You can use Cloudinary to dynamically generate an image from a given textual string with the <code>text</code> method. You can then use this textual image as any other image, for example, as an overlay for other images. Various font, color and style parameters can be specified to customize the look &amp; feel of the text before converting it to an image.</p>
          <h5>Syntax:</h5>
          <div class="example multi_code ">
           <div class="framework_links">
            <a href="#api_example_34" class="active" data-framework="ruby">Ruby</a>
            <a href="#api_example_34" class="" data-framework="php">PHP</a>
            <a href="#api_example_34" class="" data-framework="python">Python</a>
            <a href="#api_example_34" class="" data-framework="nodejs">Node.js</a>
            <a href="#api_example_34" class="" data-framework="java">Java</a>
            <a href="#api_example_34" class="" data-framework="endpoint">Endpoint</a>
            <a href="#api_example_34" class=" sample_all" data-framework="all">All</a>
           </div>
           <a class="anchor" name="api_example_34"></a>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample active" data-framework="ruby">
            <div class="framework_name">
             Ruby:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre>result = <span class="constant">Cloudinary</span>::<span class="constant">Uploader</span>.text(text, options = {})</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="php">
            <div class="framework_name">
             PHP:
            </div>
            <div class="code-holder ">
             <div class="code_inner">
              <div class="CodeRay"> 
               <div class="code">
                <pre><span class="local-variable">$result</span> = \<span class="constant">Cloudinary</span>\<span class="constant">Uploader</span>::text(<span class="local-variable">$text</span>, <span class="local-variable">$options</span> = <span class="predefined">array</span>());</pre>
               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="code_sample framework_sample" data-framework="python">
            <div class="framework_name">
             Python:
            </div>

               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>

              </div> 
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>

               </div> 
              </div> 
             </div>

           </div>

             Endpoint:
            </div>

             <div class="code_inner">

                <pre>https://api.cloudinary.com/v1_1/&lt;cloud_name&gt;/image/text</pre>
               </div>

             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <h5>Required parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>text</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The text string to generate an image for.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Optional parameters:</h5>
          <table class="md-table">
           <thead>
            <tr> 
             <th>Parameter</th> 
             <th>Type</th> 
             <th>Description</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead>
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>public_id</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The identifier that is used for accessing the generated image. If not specified, a unique identifier is generated by Cloudinary. <br><strong>Note</strong>: The public ID value for images and resources should not include a file extension. Include the file extension for <code>raw</code> files only.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>font_family</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>The name of the font family.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>font_size</td> 
             <td>Integer</td> 
             <td>Font size in points. Default: <code>12</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>font_color</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Name or RGB representation of the font's color. For example: <code>red</code> or <code>#ff0000</code>. Default: <code>black</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>font_weight</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Whether to use a <code>normal</code> or a <code>bold</code> font. Default: <code>normal</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>font_style</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Whether to use a <code>normal</code> or an <code>italic</code> font. Default: <code>normal</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>background</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Name or RGB representation of the background color of the generated image. For example: <code>red</code> or <code>#ff0000</code>. Default: <code>transparent</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>opacity</td> 
             <td>Integer</td> 
             <td>Text opacity value between 0 (invisible) and 100. Default: <code>100</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>text_decoration</td> 
             <td>String</td> 
             <td>Set to <code>underline</code> to define a line below the text. Default: <code>none</code>.</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table>
          <h5>Example:</h5>

    <span class="symbol">:public_id</span> =&gt; <span class="string"><span class="delimiter">"</span><span class="content">sample_text_image</span><span class="delimiter">"</span></span>,

    <span class="predefined">array</span>(
